Circular Letter from the Central Propaganda Department to Revolutionary Soldiers on Suppressing the Reds

The Central Propaganda Department issued a circular letter on the 26th to revolutionary soldiers on suppressing the Red bandits. The original text is as follows:

Revolutionary soldiers, esteemed comrades, for years you have devoted yourselves to fighting for the cause and serving the revolution, your magnificent achievements occupy one of the most glorious pages in Chinese revolutionary history and will forever be praised and admired by the people. Since you possess this glorious history, you must think more about how to cherish and carry it forward. Now, as the Central Government intensifies its suppression of the Red bandits, we would like to mention a few points for your consideration:

Although the uprising of the Red bandits has been short-lived, the severity of their devastation is beyond description. The provinces of Jiangxi and Hubei are currently in deep water, with burning, killing, looting, and villages reduced to ruins. No one, whether women, children, or the elderly, is spared. Social organization has been destroyed, and national culture has been ruined. If we do not act now, the disaster of national subjugation and racial extinction will be imminent. This is our earnest hope that our revolutionary soldiers will eliminate violence for the people and kill bandits for the country (1).

The country has experienced many misfortunes in recent years, which has inevitably given the Red bandits an opportunity to grow. However, the main reason lies in the instigation and direction of Soviet Russia and the baiting and support of the Comintern. Therefore, a small spark will start a prairie fire. If we do not quickly extinguish it, not only will the new country of the Three Principles of the People, which our revolutionary soldiers have won with red blood, be shaken, but also the cultural system of our Chinese nation for thousands of years will be destroyed at the hands of Red imperialism. This is our earnest hope that our revolutionary soldiers will strive to sweep away the Red atmosphere and secure the country (2).

The usual tactics of the Red bandits are to rely on dangerous obstacles and make false claims. They escape and prolong their lives. Our revolutionary soldiers should, in the spirit of knowing ourselves and the enemy, thoroughly observe the terrain, clearly understand the details, and avoid being intimidated by false claims or being careless. We must be prudent and thorough, be courageous and decisive in the face of adversity, maintain close contact, and unite without懈怠. Then, the tactics of the Red bandits will be exhausted, and the success of victory will be achieved. This is our earnest hope that our revolutionary soldiers will encourage each other and achieve success (3).

Peaceful unification is the desire of the people of the whole country. Now, the Red bandits in Jiangxi and Hubei are being suppressed. Unexpectedly, the reactionary forces have risen again, not hesitating to undermine peace and promote enemies, isolating themselves from the people. Our revolutionary soldiers have always adhered to the principles and made great contributions. At this critical moment of national crisis and survival, you can deeply understand the distinction between following and opposing the tide and be entrusted with the responsibility of being a pillar of the country. This is our earnest hope that you soldiers will recognize the great cause, dedicate your lives to the country, and face difficulties (4). Eliminating the Red bandits and stabilizing society is an important resolution of this National Conference, and it is also the common demand of our people. Our Party regards saving the people as its mission, so the likes and dislikes of the people are the likes and dislikes of our Party, and the suffering of the people is the suffering of our Party. We share their joys and sorrows and share their existence. You soldiers eat the food of the people and receive orders from the Party. You must know that if the bandits exist, the people will die; if the people die, the Party will die. The bandits and the Party-state cannot coexist. You must love the people as you love the Party, and you must love the Party as you love the people. Currently, our Party is urging the government to intensify the suppression. We still hope that you will be loyal, courageous, and vigorously eliminate this menace, so as to alleviate the hidden worries of the Party-state and relieve the people's suffering. At present, the Red bandits in Jiangxi and Hubei are being surrounded and suppressed. In recent months, many have been killed. Now, the Central Government is mobilizing a large army to encircle them in a tight spot. Capture is imminent, and destroying their nests and annihilating the bandits only awaits the final effort. This is the time for you to make meritorious deeds and serve the country. We hope that you will rise up and strive for it.

Incident of French Members Assaulting Chinese Members in the Sino-French Archaeological Expedition

The Antiquities Preservation Committee Decides on Countermeasures

Liu Fu's Questioning of the French Embassy Counselor

Since the return of the two members, Diao and Hao, to Beijing to report on the French side's breach of contract and assault during the Sino-French 19 Academic Archaeological Expedition, the entire country has been extremely indignant. The Antiquities Preservation Committee (entrusted by the Chinese Academic Societies Association), which organized the expedition, held an emergency meeting and decided to investigate the French side's breach of contract and assault. During the investigation, all operations and work of the East and West teams were suspended, and the position of team leader of the Bu An team was suspended first. A telegram was sent to team leader Chu Minyi, ordering him to send a detailed report of everything to facilitate the second step of processing. Yesterday, the representative of Xinjiang stationed in Beijing also sent a telegram to the Xinjiang Provincial Government, requesting it to temporarily strictly prohibit the team's vehicles from entering the country and to provide full protection and assistance to the Chinese team members during their travels.

The French Embassy also paid close attention to the incident of the French team members' assault. A few days ago, the embassy counselor Han Dewei specifically issued a statement with some clarifications, roughly stating that since seeing the report in the newspaper, he had tried to send a telegram to the public to inquire about the truth, but had not yet received a reply, and the truth was still unknown. Moreover, Chinese team leader Chu Minyi also expressed that whether the circumstances were as reported in the newspaper needed to be investigated before a judgment could be made. Based on reasoning, it was inevitable that people from the two countries who did not speak the same language would make such a long journey. If the allegations were true, the embassy would definitely not want to be biased. As for the statement that Bu An was a military officer, because all French people had to serve in the army, which was slightly different from the situation in China, they were actually all scholars. There may be some misunderstanding on this point. The French Embassy also issued a statement on this matter, with wording similar to that of Han Dewei

Page 12

The statement also denied that Bu An was a military officer. Liu Fu, a member of the Antiquities Preservation Committee, sent a letter to Han Dewei yesterday questioning what kind of scholar Bu An was. The original letter is as follows:

To Mr. Han Dewei:

Having read your statement in the newspapers, "As for the statement that Bu An was a military officer, because all French people have to serve in the army, which is slightly different from the situation in China, they are actually all scholars. There may be some misunderstanding," I deeply believe that a person in your position and who worships Christianity in the West would not commit one of the Ten Commandments and lie. I would like to raise two questions: (1) Since Bu An is not a military officer, why did he wear a military dress uniform at the official banquet at Sino-French University when he came to Beijing to negotiate in the summer of the 18th year, while all the other French people wore ordinary evening dress? (2) Since Bu An is "all scholars," what kind of science does he specialize in? From which university or specialized school did he graduate and what kind of degree or diploma did he obtain? In which school did he teach? In which academic institution did he serve? What works does he have and where were they published? Which famous academic societies invited him to be a member? I hope that you can clearly answer the above two points and publish them in the newspapers so that the public will not doubt your country's interpretation of the word "scholar" being "slightly different from the situation in China," which may lead to "some misunderstanding."

Respectfully,

Liu Fu

June 22

The Truth About Tobacco Prohibition in Anhui Province

Smokers Must Pay Fees to Register and Obtain Licenses

Merchants Must Pay Fees to Obtain Transportation Licenses

Bengbu Dispatch: After the establishment of the Anhui Tobacco Prohibition and Inspection Office, Director Hao Zihua immediately dispatched personnel to establish tobacco prohibition and inspection branch offices in important counties and towns by land and water. Because Hao also served as a seedling eradication committee member, he divided the tobacco-producing counties in Anhui Province into nine districts, assigning one inspection committee member to each district to specifically handle the inspection of tobacco seedlings. Each county was assigned a special commissioner, who in turn had inspectors and investigators to inspect tobacco seedlings and collect seedling taxes. The members assigned by Hao had all arrived in the counties to carry out work. Hao also arrived in Bengbu a few days ago and set up an office of the Anhui Tobacco Prohibition and Inspection Office in Tangyuan, the office in Bengbu. The decision was made to register the smoking households. It was reported that the regulation stipulated that each lamp would be charged a registration fee of four yuan and a license fee of several cents. For the transportation of opium, it was stipulated that each tael would be charged a transportation license fee and a voucher fee of a certain number of cents. After obtaining a transportation license and affixing a voucher, opium merchants could transport opium without hindrance and sell it openly. The so-called investigation and handling was nothing more than investigating and handling untaxed opium and opium merchants. Regarding the public sale of opium in Anhui Province, the Tobacco Prohibition and Inspection Office was drafting detailed regulations that would be promulgated and implemented soon. In order to ensure strict investigation and handling, the office stipulated that branch offices could be set up under the branch offices, and sub-stations could be set up under the branch offices. After the establishment of the Bengbu Tobacco Prohibition and Inspection Branch Office, the internal organization was ready to start work on the 22nd, first starting with investigating the opium dens and smoking households in the entire town in order to implement registration. During Yuan Lichen's handling of tobacco prohibition in the 17th year of the Republic, Bengbu Town received a minimum of 60,000 yuan per month in opium tax, and a maximum of 120,000 yuan. Now that the poppies in northern Anhui are being harvested in abundance, the opium tax revenue will definitely be considerable in the future. Counties in northern Anhui that produce opium have also set up tobacco prohibition and inspection branch offices one after another (June 24).

Chen Tiaoyuan Passes Wuhu to Go to Northern Anhui

To Return to the Province in About a Month

Wuhu Dispatch: The Red bandits in Anhui Province are wreaking havoc. In southern Anhui, the counties of Lang and Guang are the worst affected, while in northern Anhui, Liu'an is the most affected. Liu'an borders Henan Province, and over the years, many bandits have accumulated. The bandits in the nearby Mapu and Jinjia areas have occupied them as nests. Whenever the garrison troops are weak, they launch large-scale disturbances. The loss of life and property of the people in Liu'an is very serious. Last winter, the Red bandits colluded with the garrison troops to rebel, and the brigade commanders Chen Xiaosi and Chen Zhongfu died tragically. Recently, with the stationing of the 46th Division Yue Shengxuan's troops and the 5th Route Independent 5th Brigade Liang Guanying's troops, they have slightly restrained themselves. When Chairman Chiang went to Jiangxi to suppress the bandits, he originally intended to order the Commander of the General Reserve Army Corps, Chen Tiaoyuan, to accompany him and assist in the military operations. However, because the bandit gangs in Anhui Province should also be eliminated at the same time, Chairman Chiang sent a telegram to Chen from Wuhu, ordering him not to follow and to vigorously suppress the bandits in Anhui. Therefore, Chen decided to depart on the 24th to inspect and supervise the suppression of the Red bandits in Liuhe. When Chen passed through Wuhu, the heads of various agencies and leaders of various groups were waiting at the riverbank to welcome him. Chen's residence was set up at the Dongji Hotel. Therefore, the troops were stationed everywhere from Jiangkou to Zhongshan Road, and the security was very tight. Chen arrived at the No. 3 Company Wharf at 7:30 a.m. on the Anzhen warship. He immediately disembarked, met with the welcomers, and went straight to the Dongji Hotel to rest. In addition to the two companies of guards, those who followed him included Chief of Staff Li Erkang, Director of Staff Yao Maoxun, Adjutant Director and Head of the Public Relations Section Chen Guiting, Councilor Bai Junqing, and 24 staff adjutants. At 9:00, Chen, accompanied by Li Yao and others, went to the public stadium to inspect the artillery battalion of the 55th Division and the infantry of the 341st Regiment of the 57th Division, and delivered a speech. At noon, he attended the banquet of Yang Chunpu, a councilor of the headquarters. In the afternoon, he convened the heads of the military, police, and administrative agencies in Wuhu for a speech and gave instructions on everything. At 8:00 in the evening, he still took the Anzhen warship to set off, while the guards took the Rongchang small wheel to follow. It is estimated that after arriving in Chaoxian, he would stay for two hours to inspect the cavalry battalion of the 46th Division. In Hefei, there would be a delay of three or four days to inspect the Baixinshan troops of the 46th Division, and then go to Liu'an to inspect the divisions, inspect the defenses, and plan the suppression of the bandits. It is expected that he would return to the province in about a month. During this time, the Chairman of the Provincial Government would be represented by the Director of Civil Affairs Zhu Xi, and the duties of the Commander of the General Reserve Army Corps would be represented by the Commander of the 26th Army, Fan Xiji (24th).

Fujian Province Plans Bandit Suppression Funds

Six Measures Decided

All Currently Underway

Fuzhou Dispatch: Due to the intrusion of the Red bandits in eastern Jiangxi into the counties of Jianning, Taining, Chongan, Guangze, Shaowu, and Jiangle in northern Fujian, the Fujian Provincial Government specifically established a Military Supplies Design Committee to plan bandit suppression funds. The cases decided by the committee have now been handed over to the Provincial Government for separate execution. Here is a record of them: (1) A 25% additional tax on salt, tobacco, and alcohol has been added. The Provincial Government has telegraphed Yang Shuzhuang in Shanghai to contact Song Ziwen nearby so that it can be levied as soon as possible; (2) A 25% bandit suppression fee is collected on imports and exports from the Fuzhou and Xiamen Customs. The Provincial Government has dispatched committee member Chen Peikun to contact the Fuzhou and Xiamen tax commissioners and the two general chambers of commerce. Negotiations in Fuzhou have already made progress, and Chen is scheduled to go to Xiamen to negotiate within days; (3) Borrowing US dollar bonds accumulated by the Minjiang River Dredging Bureau. According to the bureau's reply, the bonds have not yet reached the redemption period and cannot be discounted. Moreover, according to the contract signed with the consular corps by the former Provincial Governor's Office, dredging donations cannot be used for other purposes, so the Provincial Government should find other solutions; (4) Rent collection. The Provincial Government has decided in an ad hoc meeting that all counties in the province except for bandit areas will collect one month's rent, which will be paid by the tenants and deducted from the rent. The collection methods will be determined separately; (5) Issuance of the second phase of treasury notes for 500,000 yuan. After the first phase is completed, the situation will be assessed and a decision will be made on whether to proceed; (6) Half salary payment to staff in party and government agencies. This will be temporarily postponed due to special circumstances. However, the above items are all underway and have not yet begun to generate revenue. Moreover, the upstream Liu, Lin, Qian, Lu, and Zhou troops have telegraphed to urge for payment, which is extremely urgent, so the Finance Department is facing great difficulties (23rd).

Procedure for Land Consolidation in Jiangsu Province

Sixty-One Counties in the Province to Be Organized in Six Phases

The Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau previously drafted a table of procedures for land consolidation throughout Jiangsu Province and five principles and submitted them to the Provincial Government, requesting that the counties' land survey fees be collected on behalf of the government from the 20th year of the Republic (1931) onwards in accordance with established practice. The Finance, Construction, and Civil Affairs Departments jointly reviewed and replied to the Provincial Government, and the Provincial Government Committee decided to approve it. The table of procedures and principles for land consolidation throughout the province are extracted below:

(1) For the land consolidation of the 61 counties in Jiangsu Province, with the exception of Zhenjiang and Jiangning, which have already been opened for land surveys, the work will be carried out in six phases starting from the 20th year of the Republic (1931), one year at a time, to be completed uniformly by the 30th year (1941). Phase 1 (Year 20): Zhenjiang, Jiangning, Danyang, Wujin, Wuxi, Changshu, Wu County, Kunshan, Baoshan, Jiading, Shanghai, Fengxian, Chongming; Phase 2 (Year 21): Qidong, Chuansha, Jinshan, Nanhui, Qingpu, Songjiang, Taicang, Wujiang, Haimen, Nantong, Rugao; Phase 3 (Year 22): Yangzhong, Jiangpu, Liuhe, Gaochun, Lishui, Jurong, Liyang, Jintan, Yixing, Jiangyin; Phase 4 (Year 23): Jingjiang, Dongtai, Taixing, Taixian, Jiangdu, Yizheng, Gaoyou, Xinghua, Bao Ying, Yancheng, Funing; Phase 5 (Year 24): Huaian, Huaiyin, Siyang, Lianshui, Shuyang, Guanyun, Donghai, Ganyu; Phase 6 (Year 25): Suqian, Suining, Pixian, Tongshan, Xiaoxian, Fengxian, Peixian. (2) Each county will have a preparation period of six months for carrying out land consolidation, establish a county land bureau, and train land survey personnel. The completion period for the land survey should be estimated separately according to the size of each county's area and the condition of the land, and the longest period should not exceed six years. (3) Land registration in each county should be promoted in the area that has been surveyed one year after the land survey is opened, and should be carried out one year after the completion of the land survey. (4) The technical standards for carrying out land surveys and surveying and mapping general and sub-maps and books should be determined according to the needs of the facts and the deadline for land consolidation throughout the province. (5) The expenses for carrying out land surveys and surveying and mapping general and sub-maps and books should be determined according to the actual receipts of the provincial land survey donation and the budget limit should be determined. If there is a shortfall, the following three items may be allocated to assist: 1. Interest on the balance of the land survey donation; 2. Tax increase fee; 3. Surplus funds under the registration revenue item.

The Dark Side of Tao the Bandit Serving as a Detective: Tao Hulong, a pseudo-battalion commander under the lake bandit Taibao Ashu, was captured in Shanghai by the Su Provincial Water Public Security No. 1 District on the 14th of last month through a lead and escorted to Songjiang for interrogation, as reported in the previous news. Now it is known that Tao the bandit served as a water police inspector in Zhejiang Province four years ago and lived in Tao Zhuang Town, which belonged to Jia Shan County, for a long time. Therefore, he was very familiar with the situation in Jia Shan, Jiaxing, Pinghu, and other counties in Zhejiang Province. Most of the major kidnapping cases he committed were also in Zhejiang Province. He once robbed the Lin family in Tao Zhuang, the Xin, Zhen, and other places. There are countless other kidnapping and extortion cases. This spring, after the Songjiang, Jinshan, Jia Ping, and the four counties Bandit Suppression Command offered a reward for his arrest, Tao the bandit fled to Zhejiang in mid-March. He was once arrested by the Zhejiang Provincial Water Police, but the bandit was very resourceful and bribed Shen Yongshun (aka Shen Ahai) and Fei Jincai (aka Fei Yunxiang), who are now serving as detectives in the Zhejiang Water Police (it is said that Shen and Fei robbed Qianjiawei and He Hangzhen in Jinshan County on March 7 and June 2 of last year and fled to Zhejiang after being pursued by the Water Police and the No. 4 Anti-Smuggling Brigade). They had a good relationship with Tao the bandit and also persuaded Wang Deqing, the captain of the Zhejiang Water Police Patrol and Detective Team, to release him. They also changed his name to Tao Huansan and Wang Bao recommended him as a detective in the team. Therefore, when Tao the bandit was captured in Shanghai this time, a Tao Huansan detective symbol No. 131 of the Zhejiang Inland River Water Police Bureau and a document were found on him. It is said that the Bandit Suppression Command had heard rumors of this before Tao was captured and sent a letter to the Zhejiang Provincial Water Police to investigate, but the reply denied it, saying that the bandit was still arrested in Shanghai, which can be said to be the justice of heaven.

The Civil Affairs Department commissioned Kunshan County Magistrate Pang Gao, and the High Court commissioned Taicang Judge Zhao to oversee the burning. Commissioners Pang and Zhao verified each item against the register, poured oil on it, and burned it.

County Executive and Supervisory Committee Members Selected: In the recent county party representative congress, ten candidates were selected for the executive committee, including Wei Ciyan and Dai Zhiqiang, and four candidates were selected for the supervisory committee, including Pan Zhijiu and Wu Zongqi. The nominations were immediately reported to the Provincial Reorganization Committee, which approved the following: Wei Ciyan, Dai Zhiqiang, and Lu Linxun as executive committee members; Lü Guanqun and Zhang Changjiao as alternate executive committee members; and Pan Zhijiu as supervisory committee member, with Gong Yanggao as the alternate.

Suzhou

Provincial Government Urges Payment of Business Tax: The county government received a telegram from the provincial government on the 26th, stating that it had been decided to implement the business tax starting April 1st. It was found that only Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Changshu, and other counties had implemented the tax collection, while other counties were slow to act, causing delays. The county magistrate was ordered to effectively supervise and ensure implementation within one month.

剿匪 Army Continuously Captures Bandits: The 1st Battalion, 1st Regiment of the Taihu Bandit Suppression Army, led by Battalion Commander Gao, set out to search the Binhu area of Wujiang the day before. Yesterday, in places such as the Gengqi Hamlet of the 10th District of Zexi Township, they successively captured bandits Shen Er, Shen A’tu, and Tong Tang, totaling four. They were immediately ordered to be escorted to the command headquarters in Suzhou for investigation.

Wanted Fugitives Released on Bail: Yesterday and today, the High Court issued arrest warrants for fugitives from various counties, including Li Zhizhen, accused of false accusation in Qidong; Gu Huanzhang, accused of dereliction of duty in Jiangning; Li Jingchun, accused of assault in Tongshan; and Wu Qixiang, accused of false accusation in Shanghai. They will be tried upon capture.

Changshu Jiaotong Bank Branch Manager Embezzles Funds and Is Arrested: Gu Enjin, the manager of the Changshu Jiaotong Bank, had been in office for over twenty years. Recently, the head office sent someone to replace him. Upon handover, it was discovered that Gu had embezzled over two hundred thousand yuan and fled. After the Shanghai head office learned that Gu was hiding in Suzhou, they telegraphed the Wuxian Public Security Bureau yesterday (the 26th), requesting police officers to arrest Gu at the Railway Hotel outside Changmen. He was then escorted to the local court for investigation.

Wuxi

Scandalous Police Officer Submits Resignation: Sun Rongding, the director of the 2nd Public Security Branch outside Guangfu Gate, recently enticed Ms. Tang Quanyu, a talented student from a sericulture school, to commit adultery at Room 25 of the Qitai Inn. Zou Yanliang and Wei Mei broke down the door and caught them both. When Magistrate Pan learned of this, he was furious and immediately submitted a report to the Civil Affairs Department for instructions. It is now known that Director Sun has repeatedly tried to find a way out since the incident, but without success. Realizing that his position was untenable, Director Sun submitted a resignation to Director Xu of the Public Security Bureau yesterday, which Director Xu immediately forwarded to the county government for review and approval.

Passenger Falls into River; Court Investigates: A shipping vessel from Yangku Town, Jiangyin, recently set sail to Wuxi. A passenger went out to urinate and fell into the river at Wan’an Bridge in Wuxi, resulting in death. Zheng Xiaoda, a relative of the boat owner, reported the incident to the county court for investigation. Last night (the 25th) at 6 PM, Prosecutor Du, along with Secretary Shen and investigating officers, went to the boat near Qingfeng Yarn Factory in Zhoushanbang to investigate. It was determined that the death was due to accidentally falling into the river while alive. The boat owner, Jin Fu, was ordered to prepare a coffin for collection and await identification by the deceased's family. It is also reported that the deceased was named Wang Zhenyang, from Shaqiaotougang, and that the boat owner has entrusted someone to investigate his family based on information obtained from other passengers on the boat.

普庆 Monk Arrested and Sent to Court: Puqing, a retired abbot of Longguang Temple on Mount Xishan in the county, was previously found indulging in prostitution at Wang Qiaoxian's brothel. The 5th Public Security Branch arrested him and found smoking paraphernalia and a woman named Chen Jujuan. They were both released on bail separately. Afterwards, the prosecutor's office repeatedly summoned Puqing without success, so the guarantor, Chen Baoshu, was arrested and detained. Chen Jujuan has already been sentenced by the court and is serving her sentence. It is now known that guarantor Chen Baoshu felt aggrieved at being punished for someone else's crime. Recently, he learned that Puqing was hiding in Shanghai, so he sent someone to Shanghai to search for him. The man unexpectedly encountered Puqing and immediately found a way to escort him to the train station and hand him over to the railway police. The railway police temporarily detained Puqing, while the man took the train back to Wuxi and reported to the County Court Prosecutor's Office. Chief Zhou sent several legal officers to Shanghai to escort Puqing back to Wuxi, and he arrived at the County Court yesterday morning (the 26th) at 11 AM. At 3 PM, Chief Zhou opened the court for interrogation and ordered Puqing to be detained. The guarantor, Chen Baoshu, was released.

Yangzhou

憲警處長 Director of Military Police Inspects Yangzhou: 温 Director Wen of the Military, Naval, and Air Force Headquarters' Police Department arrived in Yangzhou from Beijing on the 24th at 10 AM to inspect the new recruits of the 1st Regiment. He then gave a detailed motivational speech to the newly appointed officers of the regiment and announced the police plan, which is about to be established. The 2nd Regiment will be established immediately.

熊烈士园墓 Memorial Foundation Ceremony for Xiong Martyr's Cemetery Scheduled: The committee for preparing the Xiong Martyr's Cemetery has scheduled the foundation ceremony for the 28th at 10 AM at the purchased cemetery site. Special notices were sent to various organizations on the 25th, requesting them to send representatives to attend.

警察隊長 Police Captain Suspected of Harboring Bandits: Chen Honggao, the police captain of Lianshui County, is suspected of harboring bandits and accepting bribes from thieves. Citizens Zhu Zhenqing and others from the county have jointly filed a complaint with the Superintendent's Office, which has issued a document ordering the county magistrate to investigate the matter impartially and report back.

Gaoyou

四届縣代表 Fourth Session of County Representatives Elected: The fourth session of the County Representatives Congress has been designated by the Provincial Party Department to open on the 27th of this month. The county representatives from each district branch have now been elected, including Li Zhannan and Wang Lianzhen from the 1st District, 1st Branch; Geng Tongshu and Zhang Jinshi from the 1st District, 2nd Branch; Zhang Zhengbang and Wang Tingfan from the 1st District, 3rd Branch; Cao Ji and Dong Yunhong from the 2nd District, 1st Branch; Gao Mengqi and Wang Ti’an from the 2nd District, 2nd Branch; Lu Xingyu and Bian Yongshou from the 2nd District, 3rd Branch; Long Deyuan and Chen Deqing from the 3rd District, 1st Branch; Zheng Meishan and Li Zhiming from the 3rd District, 2nd Branch; and Ding Fengnian and others from the 3rd District, 3rd Branch, totaling seventeen people.

盜匪纵火焚燬民房 Bandits Set Fire and Burn Down Civilian House: The house of Zhu Detian, a farmer in Xiaoyin Village, 10th District of the county, was suddenly visited by six bandits armed with guns on the night before last. They demanded a large sum of money, but Zhu, having no money at home, requested an extension. After the bandits left, Zhu immediately led his family to Baoying County to take refuge temporarily. When the bandits returned at the appointed time and found the door unlocked, they became enraged and set fire to his house, causing significant damage.

Nantong

黄包车夫摀毁建設局 Rickshaw Pullers Vandalize Construction Bureau: Rickshaw pullers in Nantong vandalized the Construction Bureau due to repeated increases in vehicle taxes. On the 25th, after three representatives were arrested by Construction Bureau Director Feng Mufu and sent to the county government for release, the workers went on strike. In the afternoon, six to seven hundred rickshaw pullers stormed into the Construction Bureau and vandalized it. The county government dispatched police to suppress the riot, firing shots as a warning. However, the crowd continued to make noise until late at night before dispersing. The county government has telegraphed the province for instructions. Director Feng is currently taking refuge elsewhere.

軍政部催辦兵田案 Ministry of Military Affairs Urges Handling of Military Farmland Case: On the 25th, the Ministry of Military Affairs ordered Nantong County Magistrate Zhang to quickly recover the land price for the military farmland of the two battalions in Su Zhen and Wolf Mountain, which had been illegally occupied by the Tonghai Reclamation Company, in accordance with the clear order from the National Government. If the company is unwilling to comply, the land should be taken back and auctioned off to expedite the closure of the case.

淸查田賦標準 Standard for Investigating Land Taxes:賀 Provincial Committee Member He Liangyu came to Nantong to investigate land taxes and has formed a committee with the county government's finance bureau and local gentry to investigate the standards. It was decided that the investigation would be conducted immediately based on the land survey maps.

Pinghu

駐軍譁變續誌 Continued Report on Mutiny of Garrison Troops: The situation regarding the mutiny of the 16th Company, 4th Battalion, 7th Regiment of the Provincial Security Forces stationed in Xincang has been reported yesterday. A confirmed report from Zhapu states that at 11 AM on the 23rd, the mutinying soldiers stormed into the city through the east gate and went directly to the Public Security Bureau, seizing two Weaver rifles and one pistol. They then went to the Guangji Pawnshop and looted a large amount of jewelry, worth about four to five thousand silver dollars. Before leaving, they opened the pawnshop door and brandished a hand-held machine gun as a show of force. Residents fled in panic upon hearing the sound. The mutinying soldiers then went to Xu Tifu's house and looted several pieces of gold jewelry, shattering the windows with bullets. They also went to Tao Xiangshun, Li Da Mao, Longxing Department Store, Zhang Tongyuan, and other shops to loot. In the afternoon, they gathered at the seawall, intending to flee towards Yuyao. Coincidentally, a company of the provincial security forces dispatched from the provincial capital had arrived in Zhapu by car and immediately opened fire upon encountering the mutineers. The Haiyan Defense Corps also arrived in the Zhapu area to join the battle. At that time, the mutinying soldiers had already entered the sea on boats, but they were stranded on the coast due to the tide and were at a disadvantage in the battle. Twenty-seven were captured, five or six escaped into the mountains, four fled to the north gate, and the rest scattered. In the afternoon, two companies of the provincial guard team stationed in Pingchao County and a platoon of the provincial security forces arrived in Pinghu from Hangzhou and proceeded to Zhapu after seeing that the county town was secure. They ordered a search, which resulted in the capture of one person. The Pingchao patrol team apprehended six people, the Public Security Bureau apprehended two people, and the 5th Detachment of the Water Police apprehended four people in Xitang Bridge, along with four rifles and one pistol. The county's Cleanup Bureau apprehended two people. All were taken to the county for detention. For the time being, one company of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Forces under Bai Ji was requested to fill the defense in the Xincang area. Those killed by the mutinying soldiers included Huang Xiao'er of Huxiao Bridge and Shen Jinqiao, the owner of Yonghexiang Shop in Xincang. Those wounded by gunfire included Ma Qibin, a standing committee member of the 3rd District Party Department; Zhu Chenguang, the district chief; and Zhao Yangfeng, the owner of Yongkangtai Shop. The wounded have been sent to the hospital for treatment.

Shangyu

西華村盜刦兩家 Two Families Robbed in Xihua Village: On the night of the previous day, six or seven bandits broke into Zhao Jiaquan Tai Wine Shop in Xihua Village. All the partners awoke from their dreams but hid and dared not speak. The bandits calmly searched for more than an hour, stealing more than two hundred silver dollars, clothes, and other items. They then swarmed to Liu Rentai Grocery Store next to the Xihua Temple and looted everything, including cloth. The total loss, including silver coins, was approximately six to seven hundred dollars.

來函 Letter:

無錫戴順志函 Letter from Dai Shunzhi of Wuxi:

敬啟者 Respectfully Inform: In the Foreign News column of your newspaper on the 22nd, there was a report about a graduate of the police academy causing trouble and being detained, which is completely inconsistent with the facts. On that day, I and a friend were passing by the Bianmin Bridge in the south of the city when 江北 Jiangbei residents 虞同江 Yu Tongjiang and 徐必先 Xu Bixian were fighting. I stepped forward to persuade them, but they would not listen. The local police officers took the two men to the branch office for questioning and then transferred them to the court. This matter has nothing to do with me. Because I witnessed it at the time, I came forward to testify. After Prosecutor Du opened the court and investigated, he found that Yu Tongjiang was not injured and immediately ordered his release. It was not a graduate of the police academy who caused trouble, was detained, and released on bail. I believe the reporter misreported the facts. I am writing this letter specifically for correction and request that it be published in the Letters to the Editor column to clarify the truth. Dai Shunzhi, respectfully, 23rd.

巿立圖書館徵求圖書暫行辦法 Provisional Measures for Soliciting Books for the Municipal Library:

上海市教育局爲公佈徵求巿立圖書館圖書暫行辦法通云 The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice to announce the provisional measures for soliciting books for the Municipal Library, stating: The construction of the Municipal Library at the original site of the Zunjing Pavilion of the Confucius Temple has begun and will be completed soon. In order to collect books, the Bureau has formulated ten provisional measures for soliciting books and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval. The measures are hereby announced as follows: (1) The Bureau has formulated these provisional measures for the purpose of soliciting books for the Municipal Library. (2) Those who wish to donate published or self-printed books to the Municipal Library should first inform the Bureau of the book title, value, and contact address by letter, and the Bureau will send someone to contact them. (3) All donated books should be stamped by the donor for commemoration. (4) The Bureau will issue receipts for all donated books. (5) For a single donation of books with a value of 50 yuan or more, the Bureau will engrave the donor's name in the Municipal Library. (6) For a single donation of books with a value of 500 yuan or more, the Bureau will follow the measures in Article 5 and award a third-class commendation. (7) For a single donation of books with a value of 5,000 yuan to 10,000 yuan, the Bureau will follow the measures in Article 5 and award a second-class commendation. (8) For a single donation of books with a value of 10,000 yuan or more, the Bureau will follow the measures in Article 5 and award a first-class commendation. (9) Those who wish to sell and donate valuable books can inform the Bureau by letter as per Article 2, and the Bureau will send someone to appraise and provide a price, with the remaining items handled in accordance with Articles 3 and 4. (10) These provisional measures will be implemented after being approved and announced by the Municipal Government.

籌備第三區小學教員暑期講習會 Preparations for the Summer Training Course for Elementary School Teachers in the Third District:

江蘇省第三區小學教員暑期講習會委員會 The Summer Training Course for Elementary School Teachers in the Third District of Jiangsu Province Committee held a meeting on the 25th and 26th of this month at the Provincial Shanghai Middle School in the South City. Secretary Hou of the Education Department, Principal Zheng of Shanghai Middle School, Yuan Caihua of Qingpu, Xiang Weixian of Jinshan, Yang Binru of Nanhui, Zhu Shouru of Songjiang, Chen Zaofeng of Baoshan, Zhang Yunwu of Jiading, Cao Cheng of Fengxian, Shi Yangyong of Shanghai, and Liu Shibin of Chuansha were present. Secretary Hou presided over the meeting and Sheshi recorded the minutes. After the formalities, the chairman reported on the general outline and progress of the organization. The following was then discussed: (1) The organization plan of the committee was resolved to be organized according to the outline issued by the Education Department. (2) The term and location of the meeting were resolved to reduce the financial burden on the counties. The term was originally set for four weeks, with three hours of classes each day, but has been changed to three weeks (July 13 to August 2), with four hours of classes each day. The location will be the Junior High School Department of Shanghai Middle School at Xiaoximen. (3) The curriculum for the opening class was resolved to be four hours for Party Principles, four hours for attention to symbols, six hours for single-level teaching methods, four hours for elementary school discipline issues, six hours for agricultural and forestry education, two hours for educational administration, twelve hours for elementary school equipment (including simple methods for making elementary school equipment), eight hours for testing methods for each subject, and six lectures by celebrities. (4) The employment of lecturers and celebrity speakers was resolved to be selected and hired by the chairman, committee members, and Principal Zheng. (5) The source and distribution of funds were resolved to be four yuan per person for food and three yuan per person for lodging and miscellaneous expenses, to be shared by each county based on the number of students. The salaries of the lecturers, staff, and the cost of publications are limited to 800 yuan, to be shared equally by each county. (6) Group discussions were resolved to be handled at the discretion of the organizers. (7) The registration procedures for students were resolved to be that the list of students from each county should be sent to the meeting by July 10. All students must register one day before the start of school. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM on the 26th.

World Tennis Tournament Doubles Match is Lively

Women's Singles: 16 Players Remaining | Men's Singles: No Matches

Men's Doubles: Excitement is High | American Group Enters Third Week | Kechant and Brown (France) vs. Miki and Aoki (Japan) in a Great Battle |

London, 25th Dispatch

The Wimbledon Tennis Championships' men's singles competition has been reduced to sixteen players and is currently suspended. Today, all attention is focused on the women's singles and men's doubles.

Women's Singles Atmosphere is Tense

The women's singles has also been reduced to sixteen players. Those selected include Mrs. Van Ryn (USA), Ms. Helen Jacobs (USA), Mrs. Harper (USA). From England, there are Mrs. Godfree, Ms. Stanley, Ms. Lyttleton, and the most promising Miss Nutthall, who defeated the third-ranked German Ms. Barts 4-6, 6-0, 6-1. Ms. Lyttleton and Ms. Mudford were also surprisingly good.

Ms. Aussem Takes a Further Step

The German Ms. Aussem became the first to advance from the sixteen to the fourth week, becoming one of the final eight. Aussem won the French Open singles championship, and hopes are high for her at Wimbledon as well. Other German women's singles players selected include Ms. Krahwinkel and Mrs. Palfau

Men's Doubles is Extremely Popular

The men's doubles competition has begun. The Austrian team of Czetwertnia and Artens defeated the Argentine Davis Cup players Boyd and Zaber 0-6, 8-6, 6-4, 6-1. The South African Davis Cup players Farquharson and Kirbie, along with Spence and Raymond, entered the second week. The British Lee team, partnered with Oliff, defeated the strong Indian team of Mohan and Singh 6-0, 6-1, 6-4 after eliminating Lott.

American Men's Doubles Hopes are Limitless

American men's doubles hopes are limitless. Lott and Van Ryn have advanced to the third week, and Shields and Wood to the second week. Lott and Van Ryn won the men's doubles championship at this year's French Open.

Japanese Men's Doubles Win One and Lose One

The Japanese team of Sato Jiro and Kawachi defeated the British team of Brown and Mikael 7-5, 6-4, 6-1 today, while the team of Miki and Aoki were eliminated by Cochet and Brown with a score of 6 sets, 10-8, 6-3. This attracted the most attention.

Fierce Battle Between French and Japanese Doubles Teams

The French team of Cochet and Brown aggressively attacked the center line in the first set, causing the Japanese team to fall behind 4-2, eventually losing 6-4. Brown often used drop shots to lure the Japanese players to the net. In the second set, the French team took a 2-0 lead, but the Japanese players suddenly rallied. Miki powerfully hit groundstrokes from the baseline, while Aoki volleyed and smashed at the net, tying the score at 8-8. However, Aoki was too careless, and the ball touched the net once, resulting in a loss of the second set. In the third set, Cochet's groundstrokes for the French team fully recovered, and the diagonal shots were extremely accurate. Brown, on the other hand, killed at the net, and when the score was 4-0, Aoki's kill at the net was very effective, winning three consecutive games, but they could not continue their victory and were eventually eliminated. Cochet used drop shots and corner shots to determine the outcome. The Japanese team attacked Cochet with all their might, but he had recovered to his original form.

Local News

Wang Zhengting Arrives in Shanghai

To Attend the Polish Chargé d'Affaires' Banquet

Will Meet with Mr. Feetham This Morning

Remarks to Reporters Yesterday: Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing yesterday afternoon at 5 PM. In the evening, he attended a grand banquet hosted by the Polish Chargé d'Affaires, Mr. Weidenthal, to celebrate the signing of the Sino-Polish Treaty of Amity and Commerce. Our reporter interviewed Foreign Minister Wang yesterday to inquire about recent diplomatic matters.

Sino-American Legal Rights

Mr. Wang replied: (1) Regarding the Sino-American legal rights negotiations in Nanjing, an agreement has been made with the American ambassador to begin negotiations once the negotiation documents are sent from Washington. The American ambassador is about to go north to escape the summer heat and is expected to come to Nanjing for negotiations in the near future. As for the selection of our country's ambassador to the United States, the Ministry is considering it carefully. All external rumors are untrue.

Sino-Japanese Negotiations

(2) Regarding the Sino-Japanese legal rights negotiations, he has met with the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires, Mr. Shigemitsu, in Nanjing several times and has made concrete progress. External rumors that the Japanese side may propose a new proposal are untrue. Mr. Shigemitsu returned to Shanghai this morning (i.e., yesterday morning). The date for continued talks has not yet been decided. As for the issue of the tax rate for the Fushun coal mine, our country will definitely not agree to the Japanese side's request for a reduction. Regarding the issue of Japanese fishing boats crossing the border to fish, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Navy Department are jointly preparing the implementation of new regulations. Mr. Shigemitsu has repeatedly protested about this, but it concerns our country's sovereignty and cannot be relaxed in any way.

Recovery of Concessions

(3) Regarding the recovery of concessions, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs only issued notes to one or two relevant countries on the 22nd. The notes to the other countries are still being actively prepared. The date when the various countries will send representatives to Nanjing for formal consultations cannot be predicted until after the summer vacation, etc.

Meeting with Feetham

It is heard that Foreign Minister Wang will consult with Mr. Feetham, the advisor to the Public Works Department, regarding concession issues, as Mr. Feetham is scheduled to leave Shanghai and return to the Philippines on the 30th of this month. Mr. Wang is scheduled to meet with Mr. Feetham this morning and deliver an English speech at the graduation ceremony of St. John's University at 5 PM this afternoon. He will return to Nanjing tomorrow evening.

French Radio Station Commercial News Case

Negotiations Resolved After Ten Years: The French concession's Gujiazhai radio station was privately established by French entities and infringed upon our country's sovereignty. Our government has repeatedly protested and negotiated for more than ten years. It is now learned that the Ministry of Transportation has consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the French ambassador. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has now replied in a letter, ordering the station to only use official telegrams and weather reports from June 15th of this year and not to send or receive any other telegrams. After the Ministry of Foreign Affairs replies, it will immediately consult with the Ministry of Transportation for verification and notify the local International Telegraph Office yesterday. It is also heard that all commercial telegrams between China and France and ship telegrams will be stopped by the station and will be directly transmitted by the Sassoon House Ministry of Transportation International Radio Station receiving and transmitting office through the International Radio Station and the Wusong Radio Station. The location of the receiving and transmitting office is suitable and should be faster.

The Navy Special Party Department Requests the Recovery of Pilotage Rights

A Case of Implementing National Orders

The Navy Special Party Department, which abolished self-governing orders, believes that pilotage rights are of great importance to maritime rights and maritime administration and should be recovered urgently. Therefore, it submitted a request to the Central Party Department's Executive Committee yesterday for handling. The request stated: "The issue of national territorial waters sovereignty is as important as territorial sovereignty, and among the various aspects of territorial waters rights, pilotage rights are the most important. There are three reasons for this. First, pilotage and guidance are the responsibility of the landowner and should be the exclusive business of our nationals. Second, pilots are responsible for leading foreign ships through the sea lanes into port fortresses, warning foreigners about photography and mapping, and preventing other types of reconnaissance. Third, if foreigners are free to act as pilots, they may be used by enemy countries in wartime. Based on these three points, no country in the world would entrust pilotage rights to foreigners. However, according to Article 2 of the pilotage regulations for various ports established by Hart, the Inspector General of Customs, during the sixth year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty, 'Any Chinese citizen or citizen of a treaty country who wishes to serve as a pilot shall be permitted to do so equally.' At that time, the number of pilots in various ports of our country was reported by Hart to the Qing Dynasty Prime Minister's Office on September 10th of the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign, stating that there were a total of 203 pilots in various ports, including 103 Chinese, 6 Swedes, 2 Dutch, and 1 Austrian. This type of regulation was only implemented for one year, and foreigners already accounted for half of the number. Now, all pilots in various ports are foreigners, and their business licenses are issued by the customs. Moreover, there are many foreigners who privately act as pilots on the Yangtze River. Furthermore, during the Sino-French War in the eleventh year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, a French warship entered the Min River estuary, guided by an American pilot who was issued a license by our customs. This is recorded in Moore's International Law, and scholars of international law in various countries consider it a strange tale. At that time, the number of Chinese ships sunk and the number of people killed were so great that the country was humiliated and the army was defeated. This pilotage regulation was the main cause of this tragedy. Looking back on the past, we cannot help but tremble. The National Assembly passed a resolution to automatically abolish unequal treaties and resolutely recover all lost sovereignty. Pilotage rights are naturally among the rights that should be recovered quickly. Moreover, this regulation was originally a national order implemented by the Qing Dynasty and is not comparable to a treaty or agreement, so it can be cancelled at any time. We should immediately abolish the pilotage regulations of the sixth year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty with a national order, stipulating that no one other than Chinese citizens may serve as pilots, so as to determine sovereignty and eliminate long-standing malpractices. This will be convenient for the party. We respectfully submit this request to the Executive Committee of the Central Committee, requesting that it be forwarded to the National Government to issue an order to abolish the pilotage regulations of the sixth year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty, stipulating that no one other than Chinese citizens may serve as pilots, so as to determine sovereignty and eliminate long-standing malpractices. This will be convenient for the party. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Committee of the Central Committee."

News Yesterday Regarding the Recovery of the Yangzi Wharf

The Ministry of Transportation Sent Personnel to Shanghai to Handle the Matter

To Coordinate with the Shanghai Navigation Bureau in Recovering the Yangzi Wharf in Pudong: The Ministry of Transportation dispatched Commissioner Xu Shidan to Shanghai yesterday to coordinate with the Shanghai Navigation Bureau in handling the recovery of the Yangzi Wharf in Pudong. The reporter from China Eastern News Agency visited Mr. Xi Dingmo, the director of the Shanghai Navigation Bureau, at his private residence yesterday. Commissioner Xu, who was sent to Shanghai by the Ministry of Transportation, was also present. The interview was very detailed. The details are as follows:

History of the Wharf

Mr. Xi and Mr. Xu stated that the Yangzi Wharf in Pudong was originally a German industry. Our country severed diplomatic relations with Germany in September of the sixth year of the Republic of China due to its participation in the European War and confiscated all of the wharf's assets. The following year (the seventh year of the Republic of China), the Ministry of Transportation leased the Yangzi Wharf, along with small steamboats and all office equipment, to the Japanese company Ocean Society. At that time, the rent was 700 taels per month, which was later increased to 1,400 taels.

Accumulated Arrears Over the Years

After the Japanese company Ocean Society leased the Yangzi Wharf in the seventh year of the Republic of China, it initially paid the rent on a monthly basis without any arrears. However, starting in July of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, it stopped paying rent until April of the twentieth year, accumulating a total of 135,600 taels in arrears.

Coordinating Negotiations

In order to protect property rights, the Ministry of Transportation cancelled its lease rights in accordance with the contract. Therefore, it has dispatched Mr. Xu to Shanghai to coordinate with the Shanghai Navigation Bureau in handling the matter. It has also posted a notice from the Ministry of Transportation at the Yangzi Wharf in Pudong, informing all Chinese and foreign ships that they are prohibited from berthing at the wharf.

Reasons for Resisting Rent

The reasons why the Ocean Society resisted paying rent are quite laughable. According to the Japanese side, the Hunan Mint owed the Japanese Showa Commercial Company 385,642 taels of copper in the sixth year of the Republic of China. According to the Ocean Society, the rent for the Yangzi Wharf should be deducted from this debt. This type of reason for resisting rent, which ignores laws and regulations, is truly unheard of. The Ministry of Finance did not approve the arrears for the copper owed by the former Hunan Mint at that time, so it cannot be valid. Moreover, the former Hunan Mint's debt to the Showa Commercial Company and the Ocean Society's debt to the Ministry of Transportation cannot be discussed together. An order has been received to negotiate, and efforts will be made to handle the matter.

Japanese Stance

The Japanese Vice Consul, Mr. Shirai Yasushi, stated that the Ocean Society had acquired the debt of the Japanese Showa Commercial Company. The former Hunan Mint and the current Ministry of Transportation are both Chinese institutions and should be deducted.

Agenda for the Seventh Municipal Congress Determined

Decided to Open on July 1st

Two Consecutive Days of Meetings: The Seventh Shanghai Special Municipal Congress of the Chinese Nationalist Party is approaching. The following is a brief record of the news obtained from the secretariat of the congress:

Congress Officials

The presidium of the congress will consist of five members, one each nominated by the municipal executive committee and the municipal supervisory committee, and three additional members nominated by the congress. It is heard that the municipal executive committee has nominated Pan Gongzhan and the municipal supervisory committee has nominated Wang Yansong as chairmen. The secretary-general of the congress has been nominated by the municipal executive committee to be Tao Baichuan. The members of the representative qualification review committee will be nominated by the municipal executive committee: Huang Xuchu, Tong Xingbai, and the municipal supervisory committee: Jiang Huaisu. As for the proposal review committee, resolution sorting committee, and congress declaration drafting committee, etc., they will all be nominated by the congress. It is not yet certain at present.

Congress Agenda

The congress is expected to last two days. On the first day, July 1st, the opening ceremony will be held in the morning, and representatives from the party, government, and military will report on their past work. In the afternoon, new executive and supervisory committee members will be elected. In the evening, the municipal executive committee will host a banquet for all the representatives. On the second day, July 2nd, proposals will be discussed in the morning and afternoon, and the closing ceremony will be held. If the time is not enough to finish, it may be extended by one day. The deadline for proposals has now been extended by two days, and the deadline for representative registration is set for noon on the 30th.

Congress Organization

The organizational law of the representative congress has been approved by the central government. The following is a special record of it: Article 1: Representatives attending the municipal representative congress shall be selected and sent by the party departments of each district and the directly subordinate district sub-departments of the city. Article 2: The presidium of the municipal representative congress shall consist of five members, two nominated by the municipal executive committee and three nominated by the attending representatives. Municipal executive committee members who are nominated as members of the presidium may enjoy all the powers of a chairman when serving as the chairman of the meeting, but when electing municipal executive committee members and supervisory committee members, the chairman should be nominated from among the members of the presidium nominated by the attending representatives. Article 3: The secretariat of the municipal representative congress shall have one secretary-general, four clerks, four scribes, two stenographers, and six staff members, all of whom shall be nominated by the municipal executive committee and concurrently serve as existing staff members of the municipal party department. Article 4: The representative qualification review committee shall be organized by the municipal executive committee and the municipal supervisory committee. Its number shall be determined to be three. Article 5: The proposal review committee, declaration drafting committee, and resolution sorting committee shall all be nominated by the congress. Their number shall be determined to be three. Article 6: The above-mentioned committees shall each nominate a chairman. Article 7: The representative qualification review committee shall be established and convene daily meetings during the re-election in each district. Representatives who pass the review shall be given attendance certificates immediately. The results of the review shall be announced one day before the congress, and the reasons for the disqualification of unqualified representatives shall be given. Article 8: Proposals shall be compiled into the agenda in the following order: (1) Proposals from the municipal executive committee (2) Proposals from the party departments of each district and the directly subordinate district sub-departments (3) Proposals submitted or introduced by each representative. Article 9: The powers of the municipal representative congress shall be in accordance with the provisions of Article 45 of the General Regulations, which are to accept and adopt the report of the municipal executive committee, to decide on the direction of the city's party affairs, and to elect the municipal executive committee members and supervisory committee members. Article 10: The date of convocation and the duration of the municipal representative congress shall be determined by the municipal executive committee. Article 11: The municipal representative congress shall be valid only if more than two-thirds of the total number of municipal representatives are present. Article 12: The deliberations of the municipal representative congress shall be decided by a majority vote. In the event of a tie, the chairman shall decide. Article 13: The representatives elected by the party departments of each district and the directly subordinate sub-departments shall register no later than two days before the congress and present their party cards and election certificates to the representative qualification review committee for verification. Article 14: Representatives must first present their attendance certificates to the conference staff for verification before entering the meeting hall. Article 15: Municipal executive committee members and supervisory committee members may attend the congress but only have the right to speak. Article 16: The rules of procedure of the Third National Congress of Representatives shall apply to the rules of procedure of the municipal representative congress. Article 17: This organizational law shall be implemented after being approved by the municipal executive committee and submitted to the central government for approval.

News Yesterday After the Dissolution of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce

The Social Bureau Ordered a Stop to Business Suspension

Zhang and Zheng Responded to the Social Bureau to Explain: The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has been actively preparing for the establishment of a branch office since the Social and Public Security Bureaus jointly sent personnel to take over the Wusong Chamber of Commerce. It has been internally decided that the director of the future branch office will be Mr. Zhang Yuchi, the manager of the Wusong Wansheng Sauce Garden. Mr. Zhang was formerly a standing committee member of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce and enjoys a high reputation in the Wusong business community, so he is well-qualified for the position. The Social Bureau, having heard that businessmen in the Songzhen area were using business suspension as a form of passive resistance, ordered the former standing committee members of the Song Chamber of Commerce, Zhang Yuchi and Zheng Shushan, on the previous day to be responsible for persuasion and to prevent such actions in advance. After receiving the order, Zhang and Zheng submitted a response to the Social Bureau yesterday. The Social Bureau's order and the letter from the two standing committee members are transcribed below:

Social Bureau Order

Order No. 11611 to Zhang Zengjie and Zheng Shushan: Upon investigation, the former Wusong Chamber of Commerce has not been reorganized due to its defiance of laws and regulations. The former president of the chamber of commerce, Zheng Shushan, has also been accused of fraud. The Social and Public Security Bureaus have jointly taken over the chamber and ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to organize a branch office as soon as possible to continue to take responsibility and properly clear things up. It is now found in today's newspapers that merchants in the area are using the excuse of business suspension to make demands. At a time when military operations are underway at the front, there is concern that some people may use this as an opportunity to incite chaos and disrupt public order. In addition to sending a letter to the Public Security Bureau ordering strict prevention in the area, this order is issued to the merchants to be responsible for persuasion and to prevent such actions in advance. Director of the Bureau, Pan Gongzhan.

Zhang and Zheng's Response

Report Regarding the Response: On the 24th of this month, we received Order No. 11611 from your bureau, which stated (omitted). Upon investigation, since the proposal to establish a branch office in Wusong was made, all the merchants in the town have been in an uproar. Initially, they asked that the order be revoked, and then they said that the matter was worth fighting for. Zengjie and others, as standing committee members, were caught in the middle. In fact, they have been working for many years and are inevitably exhausted. Their efforts to reduce the burden are only aimed at reducing their own burden. Once they are fortunate enough to receive the strict order to hand over the duties, they would gladly accept the responsibility even if they are reprimanded. However, there would be many obstacles within, and the criticism would lead to agitation and a mixture of people. For a moment, they felt that it was difficult to move forward or retreat. Zengjie and others tried to persuade them again and again, but they were unable to reach an agreement. Fortunately, the district officials helped them in many ways to prevent problems from arising. However, in the end, they were still responsible for petitioning to achieve their goals. Because of this, the district officials had already taken preventive measures before your Excellency's order, helping Zengjie and others to prevent problems from arising. As for the case in which Shushan was accused, Shushan had not heard of it before. On the 17th of this month, he suddenly saw the report in the newspaper. The plaintiff did not understand the truth and was being manipulated by others. He corrected it in the original newspaper on the 18th. When your committee came to the meeting, the questioning about this case was very detailed, and the original draft of the presentation to the province was taken back to be presented to your Excellency. As the previous reasons were ordered, they are now being inspected and sent for review together. Respectfully submitted to the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, Pan Gongzhan. Submitted by Zhang Zengjie and Zheng Shushan, June 26th.

The Anti-Opium Investigation Office was Established Yesterday

A Letter to Military and Police Agencies for Verification: According to the Far East News Agency, the Anti-Opium Committee, based on the resolution of the Fifth Plenary Session to ban opium completely in six years and in accordance with Article 11 of the Implementing Law of the Anti-Opium Law, established anti-opium investigation offices in important provinces by land and sea to inspect opium transportation matters. The Jiangsu-Shanghai Anti-Opium Investigation Office was formally established yesterday (26th). Its office is located at Beishun Zhengli, Huaxing Road, Zhabei. The inspection soldiers are stationed at the North Railway Station (the former inspection office of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters). The director is Deng Yixin. The public letter from the office to the military and police agencies in the area yesterday is transcribed as follows: "Respectfully, we hereby forward the letter from the Jiangsu-Shanghai Anti-Opium Investigation Office, Order No. 25, which states: 'We hereby appoint Deng Yixin as the director of the Zhabei Anti-Opium Investigation Office of this office. This order.' And a seal with the inscription 'Seal of the Jiangsu-Shanghai Zhabei Anti-Opium Investigation Office' was issued. Having received this order, the director of this office has located a building at No. 6, Beishun Zhengli, Huaxing Road, Zhabei, for use as an office. The seal was officially put into use on the 26th of this month. In addition to reporting to the authorities, we hereby send this letter for your verification. (Omitted below)"

Cancellation of Tobacco and Alcohol License Collection Offices

The Jiangsu Stamped Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau, managed directly by the government, issued a special notice yesterday announcing the abolition of the collection offices in compliance with orders, stating: "Following the Finance Ministry's instruction No. 29724 (Yin Zi), regarding the request from the Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau for instructions, it was reported that the sudden abolition of commercial contracting and the change to commissioned management for the province's tobacco and alcohol collection offices presented practical difficulties. Permission was granted for a temporary tender commission system in the 18th year (of the Republic), and in the 19th year, revisions to the regulations and adjustments to the quota were approved for continued implementation. It is noted that the tender commission was originally a transitional expedient. Now that tobacco and alcohol taxation is undergoing active reorganization, all collection offices in the province should immediately abolish the tender method starting from the 20th year. The Bureau should carefully select capable personnel to take over the positions, thoroughly reforming the system to bring about improvements. Therefore, the Bureau is hereby instructed to promptly deliberate on specific measures and submit them for review and approval without delay. This instruction is to be followed accordingly." Upon receiving this, and after considering the situation and coordinating measures, a report was submitted to the Ministry, which approved the abolishment of all existing tobacco and alcohol monopoly fee, license tax, and other collection offices in the province starting from the 20th year. Instead, 32 monopoly collection sub-bureaus and 10 license tax collection sub-bureaus will be established and staffed with carefully selected personnel to directly collect taxes. These measures have already been implemented. In addition to printing and distributing notices to the various collection sub-bureaus for posting, a copy of the notice is enclosed for your association's reference and dissemination to all tobacco and alcohol merchant guilds for their information.

The Shanghai Baochuan Chongqi Taijia Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Sub-bureau in Jiangsu had previously been managed by contractors. Recently, the Jiangsu Stamped Tobacco and Alcohol Bureau implemented a system of abolishing contractor management and switching to individual collection, appointing Gu Daosheng as the director of the Shanghai Baochuan Chongqi Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Bureau, effective from July 1st. The main bureau remains in Shanghai, with a branch bureau in each of the other four counties. The Shanghai area's contractor-managed tax collection began in the 4th year of the Republic. In the 19th year, the five counties of Shanghai Baochuan Chongqi paid over 90,000 yuan to the Jiangsu province quota. It is rumored that after the change to individual collection, the tax revenue budget is expected to increase by 40%.

The Municipal Council's Farewell to Mr. Feetham

Yu Qiaqing gave an earnest speech. The two volumes of the report by Judge Feetham, advisor to the Shanghai Municipal Council, have been finalized. Mr. Feetham is scheduled to set sail for home on the 30th of this month. The directors and key staff of the Municipal Council hosted a farewell banquet for him at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund last night at 8:30 PM. Many speeches were given amid the clinking of glasses. The following is the farewell speech by Director Yu Qiaqing:

"Judge Feetham is a British legal scholar. His thinking, knowledge, talent, and experience are all admirable and convincing. The Municipal Council specially hired him to come to Shanghai to investigate, research, and seek solutions to the problems of the concessions, resulting in seven volumes of reports. The issue of the concessions, which has persisted for over eighty years, has been addressed by one person in a short period of time, determining its solutions. It is not realistic to expect perfection and unobstructed implementation, but it is indeed commendable that such a magnificent work has been produced in such a short period of half a year, which is admired by my colleagues and the people of our country. Tonight, the Municipal Council hosts a farewell banquet for Judge Feetham at the Cathay Hotel, and we are deeply honored to be the hosts. Looking back to the evening of February 12th last year, we held a farewell banquet for Mr. Collins here. Judge Feetham was present at that time. Time flies quickly, and it has already been seventeen months. The scenes and circumstances of today evoke feelings of both nostalgia and appreciation for the present moment. This is why the ancients would hold nighttime gatherings with candles. The chairman has asked me to offer a word to Judge Feetham, and I cannot refuse. I believe what I want to say is the same as what I said to Mr. Collins. However, I am moved by the fact that U.S. President Hoover issued a statement from the White House on the 20th of this month, advocating a one-year moratorium on war debts, which was greeted with thunderous applause around the world. The international market, which was on the verge of collapse, was instantly revitalized. One word is worth a thousand pounds. Britain has helped in the past, and France is following suit. Past misunderstandings have dissipated, and the cooperation of the world's people is enough to promote Sino-foreign cooperation in Shanghai. When Judge Feetham first came to Shanghai, he said that the prosperity of Shanghai lies in its sustainability. I would like to add to his meaning: it should also be for even greater progress. We can hope for the most recent step, that is, all of humanity should maintain the prosperity of the world and strive for even greater progress. However, to achieve this goal, we should pay attention to the following: in Shanghai, we should seek Sino-foreign cooperation without hindering sovereignty; in the world, we should seek human cooperation under the premise of national self-determination. If this is possible, a world of great harmony will not be far off. Farewell, Judge Feetham! Take care and cherish yourself. We colleagues will not fail to live up to the judge's expectations and make Shanghai's prosperity even more flourishing." Shanghai, June 26th, 20th year of the Republic of China, Yu Qiaqing
