Society News

Marshal Foch's War Memoirs

— Translated by Gu Angruo

However, although the German army did not achieve a strategic victory in this war, the war in this area could be resumed at any time. The enemy could use submarines to harass the nearby sea and cut off the Allied forces' communications with Britain, isolating the British Isles and rendering them helpless. At the same time, they could use large numbers of troops to directly approach the coast of the strait at the cost of great sacrifice. Therefore, the position of the Allied forces has not yet turned from danger to safety.

Our army's loss of many places allowed the German army to occupy Mount Kemmel, and the Allied defense line's northern shield, Mount Flanter, was in imminent danger. If our defense line was to avoid wavering, Mount Flanter had to be defended with all our might. I therefore ordered Commander Mitry not only to consolidate the defenses of Mount Flanter, but also to deploy defenses to the foothills to prevent the enemy from encircling the summit and sneaking through the waist of the mountain. On May 4, the northern detachment's local operations made considerable progress in this regard.

The Battle of Flanter also had the result that the Pesinay coal region was also subjected to German artillery fire. The miners experienced serious unrest, and the coal needed by the armory and railways was greatly affected. Fortunately, with the efforts of the British army and the French liaison officer stationed at the British army headquarters, this situation was remedied.

The Allied forces' strength was greatly reduced as a result of the Battle of Flanter. The British army's reserves had already been used up, and ten divisions of French reserves had been transferred to help in the war.

I and General Haig agreed to transfer the British reserves withdrawn from the front to the peaceful area of the French line and hand them over to Commander Petain for reorganization. The French army also withdrew a portion to replenish its reserves, but this transfer could only be implemented slowly. Commander Petain first incorporated the four divisions of the British army's Ninth Army Group into the French Sixth Army and transferred them to the Kron Lovoer Line in mid-May for defense.

The Battle of Flanter lasted for a month, and the French army's deployment lost its equilibrium. At the beginning of May, the French army had forty-seven divisions north of the Arras River (twenty-three divisions at the front and twenty-four divisions in reserve). From the Arras River to the Swiss border, the defense line was guarded by only fifty-five divisions, that is, forty-three divisions at the front and twelve divisions in reserve. Commander Petain asked me to pay attention to the dangers posed by this situation.

The heavy losses suffered by the British army could not be ignored, but the enemy had the possibility of attacking again between the Arras River and the Leie River. Moreover, because this line was very close to the target of the decisive battle, victory or defeat had a great impact on the Allied forces. I therefore maintained four divisions north of the Somme River and deployed the same number of troops south of the Somme River. However, I did not change the transfer of troops to support the northern detachment.

At the same time, I made every effort to deploy American troops to benefit the French army commander's military affairs. The American First Division had already entered the defense line of the French First Army on April 26, and the battle on May 28 immediately captured the village of Contigny, proving that the American army's combat effectiveness was not weak. I asked Commander Pershing to immediately transfer the 26th, 42nd, and Second Divisions to the front, and to leave the American infantry 32nd, Third, and Fifth Divisions as reinforcements for the French army. I further asked him to send American airmen to French air force units for practice and to reduce the workload of French air force personnel. (To be continued)

The Progress of the Himalayan Climbing Team

Advancing along the glacier to the summit: A report from Garhwal states that Mr. Smith and his party are currently climbing Mount Kamet (25,431 feet) in the Himalayas. The following report, dated seven days ago, has arrived in Garhwal. It is said that the climbing team arrived at the front of the Eastern Kamet Glacier on the 6th, and the entire team is in good health. The climbing base unit departed from Niti, near the valley of Lenwoni, the last village in the climbing route, on the 5th, accompanied by thirty porters and thirty yaks carrying food supplies. These yaks appear brave, but are actually very gentle. When loaded, they are easily startled and run away, which causes difficulty. However, there was no major loss of goods. They advanced with a steady pace along the steep slope. As they moved away from the village of Niti, the terrain gradually became barren and rocky. The group plans to depart from Fishtiab on the 8th with forty porters and climb along the Eastern Kamet Glacier to a point at 16,800 feet. The next day, they will reduce the number of porters and advance to a point at 18,500 feet, where they will set up a camp. Messrs. Bori and Piman will return to Fishtiab first after transporting the remaining supplies with the porters. Both gentlemen have gradually become accustomed to the rapid changes in climate and terrain and should have no difficulty transporting the remaining supplies. If the current good weather continues, the fourth base will be set up at a location of 22,500 feet in two weeks. It is planned to transport ten days' worth of food supplies to the fourth camp. After digging caves in the ice and snow at that location to conserve energy, they will then advance to higher altitudes and establish a simple camp to launch an assault on the highest peak. Also, Mischief Gorge, said to be 2,000 feet deep, is suspicious according to our survey. The natives in the group are practicing climbing glaciers with ropes, etc. Mr. Girilai is also measuring the blood pressure of the group members. People in the lower realms are spying on us and will be surprised that we have grown long beards and hair, becoming barbarians in the sky dome. We have a phonograph and abundant food supplies. We are very happy, it is said.
